Epstein, a proponent of <a href="/wiki/Sabremetrics" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabremetrics">sabremetrics</a> and one of the architects of the <a href="/wiki/2004_World_Series" title="2004 World Series">2004</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Series" title="2007 World Series">2007 World Series</a> championships in Boston, brought along <a href="/wiki/Jed_Hoyer" title="Jed Hoyer">Jed Hoyer</a> from the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">Padres</a> to fill the role of GM and hired <a href="/wiki/Dale_Sveum" title="Dale Sveum">Dale Sveum</a> as manager. Although the team had a dismal 2012 season, losing 101 games (the worst record since 1966), it was largely expected. The youth movement ushered in by Epstein and Hoyer began as longtime fan favorite Kerry Wood retired in May, followed by <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Dempster" title="Ryan Dempster">Ryan Dempster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geovany_Soto" title="Geovany Soto">Geovany Soto</a> being traded to <a href="/wiki/2012_Texas_Rangers_season" title="2012 Texas Rangers season">Texas</a> at the All-Star break for a group of minor league prospects headlined by <a href="/wiki/Christian_Villanueva" title="Christian Villanueva">Christian Villanueva</a>, but also included little thought of <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Hendricks" title="Kyle Hendricks">Kyle Hendricks</a>. The development of Castro, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Rizzo_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthony Rizzo (baseball)">Anthony Rizzo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darwin_Barney" title="Darwin Barney">Darwin Barney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brett_Jackson" title="Brett Jackson">Brett Jackson</a> and pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Samardzija" title="Jeff Samardzija">Jeff Samardzija</a>, as well as the replenishing of the minor-league system with prospects such as <a href="/wiki/Javier_Baez" class="mw-redirect" title="Javier Baez">Javier Baez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Almora" title="Albert Almora">Albert Almora</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Soler" title="Jorge Soler">Jorge Soler</a> became the primary focus of the season, a philosophy which the new management said would carry over at least through the 2013 season.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anthony_Rizzo_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Anthony_Rizzo_2012.jpg/180px-Anthony_Rizzo_2012.jpg" width="180" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Anthony_Rizzo_2012.jpg/270px-Anthony_Rizzo_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Anthony_Rizzo_2012.jpg/360px-Anthony_Rizzo_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="2200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anthony_Rizzo_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of two Cubs building blocks, Anthony Rizzo, swinging in the box.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/2013_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2013 Chicago Cubs season">2013 season</a> resulted in much as the same the year before. Shortly before the trade deadline, the Cubs traded <a href="/wiki/Matt_Garza" title="Matt Garza">Matt Garza</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a> for <a href="/wiki/Mike_Olt" title="Mike Olt">Mike Olt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Edwards_Jr." title="Carl Edwards Jr.">Carl Edwards Jr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Ramirez" class="mw-redirect" title="Neil Ramirez">Neil Ramirez</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Justin_Grimm" title="Justin Grimm">Justin Grimm</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, the Cubs sent <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Soriano" title="Alfonso Soriano">Alfonso Soriano</a> to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> for minor leaguer <a href="/wiki/Corey_Black" title="Corey Black">Corey Black</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The mid season fire sale led to another last place finish in the NL Central, finishing with a record of 66-96. Although there was a five-game improvement in the record from the year before, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Rizzo_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthony Rizzo (baseball)">Anthony Rizzo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Starlin_Castro" title="Starlin Castro">Starlin Castro</a> seemed to take steps backward in their development. On September 30, 2013, <a href="/wiki/Theo_Epstein" title="Theo Epstein">Theo Epstein</a> made the decision to fire manager <a href="/wiki/Dale_Sveum" title="Dale Sveum">Dale Sveum</a> after just two seasons at the helm of the Cubs. The regression of several young players was thought to be the main focus point, as the front office said Sveum would not be judged based on wins and losses. In two seasons as skipper, Sveum finished with a record of 127\xe2\x80\x93197.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2013 season was also notable as the Cubs drafted future Rookie of the Year and MVP <a href="/wiki/Kris_Bryant" title="Kris Bryant">Kris Bryant</a> with the second overall selection.\n</p><p>On November 7, 2013, the Cubs hired <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> bench coach <a href="/wiki/Rick_Renteria" title="Rick Renteria">Rick Renteria</a> to be the 53rd manager in team history.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Cubs finished the <a href="/wiki/2014_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2014 Chicago Cubs season">2014 season</a> in last place with a 73-89 record in Renter\xc3\xada\'s first and only season as manager.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Despite the poor record, the Cubs improved in many areas during 2014, including rebound years by Anthony Rizzo and Starlin Castro, ending the season with a winning record at home for the first time since 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and compiling a 33\xe2\x80\x9334 record after the All-Star Break. However, following unexpected availability of Joe Maddon, the Cubs relieved Renter\xc3\xada of his managerial duties on October 31, 2014. During the season, the Cubs drafted <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Schwarber" title="Kyle Schwarber">Kyle Schwarber</a> with the fourth overall selection.\n</p><p>Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Banks" title="Ernie Banks">Ernie Banks</a> died of a heart attack on January 23, 2015, shortly before his 84th birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-Attack_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Attack-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The 2015 uniform carried a commemorative #14 patch on both its home and away jerseys in his honor.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2015-present:_Championship_run">2015-present: Championship run</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2015_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2015 Chicago Cubs season">2015 Chicago Cubs season</a></div>\n<p>On November 2, 2014, the Cubs announced that <a href="/wiki/Joe_Maddon" title="Joe Maddon">Joe Maddon</a> had signed a five-year contract to be the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chicago_Cubs_managers" title="List of Chicago Cubs managers">54th manager</a> in team history.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On December 10, 2014, Maddon announced that the team had signed free agent <a href="/wiki/Jon_Lester" title="Jon Lester">Jon Lester</a> to a six-year, $155 million contract. Many other trades and acquisitions occurred during the off season. The opening day lineup for the Cubs contained five new players including center fielder <a href="/wiki/Dexter_Fowler" title="Dexter Fowler">Dexter Fowler</a>. Rookies <a href="/wiki/Kris_Bryant" title="Kris Bryant">Kris Bryant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Addison_Russell" title="Addison Russell">Addison Russell</a> were in the starting lineup by mid-April, and rookie <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Schwarber" title="Kyle Schwarber">Kyle Schwarber</a> was added in mid-June. On August 30, <a href="/wiki/Jake_Arrieta" title="Jake Arrieta">Jake Arrieta</a> threw a no hitter against the Los Angeles Dodgers.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The Cubs finished the 2015 season in third place in the NL Central, with a record of 97\xe2\x80\x9365, the third best record in the majors and earned a wild card berth. On October 7, in the <a href="/wiki/2015_National_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2015 National League Wild Card Game">2015 National League Wild Card Game</a>, Arrieta pitched a complete game shutout and the Cubs defeated the <a href="/wiki/2015_Pittsburgh_Pirates_season" title="2015 Pittsburgh Pirates season">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> 4\xe2\x80\x930.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Cubs defeated the Cardinals in the <a href="/wiki/2015_National_League_Division_Series" title="2015 National League Division Series">NLDS</a> three-games-to-one, qualifying for a return to the <a href="/wiki/National_League_Division_Series" title="National League Division Series">NLCS</a> for the first time in 12 years, where they faced the <a href="/wiki/2015_New_York_Mets_season" title="2015 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a>. This was the first time in franchise history that the Cubs had clinched a playoff series at Wrigley Field.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> However, they were swept in four games by the Mets and were unable to make it to their first World Series since <a href="/wiki/1945_World_Series" title="1945 World Series">1945</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2016_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2016 Chicago Cubs season">2016 Chicago Cubs season</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3205" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Cubs_celebrate_after_winning_the_2016_World_Series._(30709972906).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Cubs celebrate after winning the <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series" title="2016 World Series">2016 World Series</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Before the season, in an effort to shore up their lineup, free agents <a href="/wiki/Ben_Zobrist" title="Ben Zobrist">Ben Zobrist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Heyward" title="Jason Heyward">Jason Heyward</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Lackey" title="John Lackey">John Lackey</a> were signed.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> To make room for the Zobrist signing, <a href="/wiki/Starlin_Castro" title="Starlin Castro">Starlin Castro</a> was traded to the Yankees for <a href="/wiki/Adam_Warren_(baseball)" title="Adam Warren (baseball)">Adam Warren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Ryan_(baseball)" title="Brendan Ryan (baseball)">Brendan Ryan</a>, the latter of whom was released a week later.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;VP9 (360P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;VP9 360P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;360p.vp9.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;640&quot; data-height=&quot;360&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;717768&quot; data-framerate=&quot;29.97&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:The 2016 World Series Champion href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/The_2016_World_Series_Champion_Chicago_Cubs.webm" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_2016_World_Series_Champion_Chicago_Cubs.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2016 Champions visit the White House in January 2017</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chicago_Cubs_with_President_Trump.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Chicago_Cubs_with_President_Trump.jpg/220px-Chicago_Cubs_with_President_Trump.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Chicago_Cubs_with_President_Trump.jpg/330px-Chicago_Cubs_with_President_Trump.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Chicago_Cubs_with_President_Trump.jpg/440px-Chicago_Cubs_with_President_Trump.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1597" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chicago_Cubs_with_President_Trump.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2016 Champions visit the White House in June 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>In a season that included a no-hitter on April 21 by Jake Arrieta,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> the Cubs finished with the best record in Major League Baseball and won their first <a href="/wiki/National_League_Central" title="National League Central">National League Central</a> title since the <a href="/wiki/2008_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2008 Chicago Cubs season">2008 season</a>, winning by 17.5 games. The team also reached the 100-win mark for the first time since <a href="/wiki/1935_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="1935 Chicago Cubs season">1935</a> and won 103 total games, the most wins for the franchise since <a href="/wiki/1910_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="1910 Chicago Cubs season">1910</a>. The Cubs defeated the <a href="/wiki/2016_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="2016 San Francisco Giants season">San Francisco Giants</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2016_National_League_Division_Series" title="2016 National League Division Series">National League Division Series</a> and returned to the <a href="/wiki/2016_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2016 National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a> for the second year in a row, where they defeated the <a href="/wiki/2016_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2016 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> in six games. This was their first NLCS win since the series was created in 1969. The win earned the Cubs their first World Series appearance since <a href="/wiki/1945_World_Series" title="1945 World Series">1945</a> and a chance for their first World Series win since <a href="/wiki/1908_World_Series" title="1908 World Series">1908</a>. Coming back from a three-games-to-one deficit, the Cubs defeated the <a href="/wiki/2016_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2016 Cleveland Indians season">Cleveland Indians</a> in seven games in the <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series" title="2016 World Series">2016 World Series</a>, They were the first team to come back from a three-games-to-one deficit since the <a href="/wiki/1985_Kansas_City_Royals_season" title="1985 Kansas City Royals season">Kansas City Royals</a> in <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Series" title="1985 World Series">1985</a>. On November 4, the city of Chicago held a victory parade and rally for the Cubs that began at Wrigley Field, headed down Lake Shore Drive, and ended in <a href="/wiki/Grant_Park_(Chicago)" title="Grant Park (Chicago)">Grant Park</a>. The city estimated that over five million people attended the parade and rally, which made it one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_peaceful_gatherings_in_history" class="mw-redirect" title="List of largest peaceful gatherings in history">largest recorded gatherings in history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2017_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2017 Chicago Cubs season">2017 Chicago Cubs season</a></div>\n<p>In an attempt to be the first team to repeat as World Series champions since the Yankees in <a href="/wiki/1998_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1998 New York Yankees season">1998</a>, <a href="/wiki/1999_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1999 New York Yankees season">1999</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2000_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2000 New York Yankees season">2000</a>, the Cubs struggled for most of the first half of the <a href="/wiki/2017_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2017 Chicago Cubs season">2017 season</a>, never moving more than four games over .500 and finishing the first half two games under .500. On July 15, the Cubs fell to a season-high 5.5 games out of first in the NL Central. The Cubs struggled mainly due to their pitching as Jake Arrieta and Jon Lester struggled and no starting pitcher managed to win more than 14 games (four pitchers won 15 games or more for the Cubs in 2016). The Cub offense also struggled as Kyle Schwarber batted near .200 for most of the first half and was even sent to the minors. However, the Cubs recovered in the second half of the season to finish 22 games over .500 and win the NL Central by six games over the <a href="/wiki/2017_Milwaukee_Brewers_season" title="2017 Milwaukee Brewers season">Milwaukee Brewers</a>. The Cubs pulled out a five-game <a href="/wiki/2017_National_League_Division_Series" title="2017 National League Division Series">NLDS</a> series win over the <a href="/wiki/2017_Washington_Nationals_season" title="2017 Washington Nationals season">Washington Nationals</a> to advance to the NLCS for the third consecutive year. For the second consecutive year, they faced the <a href="/wiki/2017_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2017 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Dodgers</a>. This time, however, the Dodgers defeated the Cubs in five games.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2018_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2018 Chicago Cubs season">2018 Chicago Cubs season</a></div>\n<p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/2018_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2018 Chicago Cubs season">2018 season</a>, the Cubs made several key free agent signings to bolster their pitching staff. The team signed starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Yu_Darvish" title="Yu Darvish">Yu Darvish</a> to a six-year, $126 million contract and veteran closer <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Morrow" title="Brandon Morrow">Brandon Morrow</a> to two-year, $21-million contract,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> in addition to <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Chatwood" title="Tyler Chatwood">Tyler Chatwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Cishek" title="Steve Cishek">Steve Cishek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> However, the Cubs struggled to stay healthy throughout the season. <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Rizzo" title="Anthony Rizzo">Anthony Rizzo</a> missed much of April due to a back injury,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and Bryant missed almost a month due to shoulder injury.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> However, Darvish, who only started eight games in 2018, was lost for the season due to elbow and triceps injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Morrow also faced two injuries before the team ruled him out for the season in September.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The team maintained first place in their division for much of the season. The injury-depleted only went 16\xe2\x80\x9311 during September, which allowed the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a>, to finish with the same record. The Brewers defeated the Cubs in a tie-breaker game to win the Central Division and secure the top-seed in the National League.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The Cubs subsequently lost to the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2018_National_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2018 National League Wild Card Game">2018 National League Wild Card Game</a> for their earliest playoff exit in three seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ballpark">Ballpark</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wrigley_Field_and_Wrigleyville">Wrigley Field and Wrigleyville</span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:354px;max-width:354px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:352px;max-width:352px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Fans_descend_on_Wrigley_Field_for_World_Series_Game_3._(30642800165).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Fans_descend_on_Wrigley_Field_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830642800165%29.jpg/350px-Fans_descend_on_Wrigley_Field_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830642800165%29.jpg" width="350" height="167" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Fans_descend_on_Wrigley_Field_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830642800165%29.jpg/525px-Fans_descend_on_Wrigley_Field_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830642800165%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Fans_descend_on_Wrigley_Field_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830642800165%29.jpg/700px-Fans_descend_on_Wrigley_Field_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830642800165%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5060" data-file-height="2421" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a> (exterior) \xe2\x80\x94 Game 3 of the <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series" title="2016 World Series">2016 World Series</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:352px;max-width:352px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Wrigley_Field_is_ready_for_World_Series_Game_3._(30525773952).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Wrigley_Field_is_ready_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830525773952%29.jpg/350px-Wrigley_Field_is_ready_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830525773952%29.jpg" width="350" height="233" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Wrigley_Field_is_ready_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830525773952%29.jpg/525px-Wrigley_Field_is_ready_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830525773952%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Wrigley_Field_is_ready_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830525773952%29.jpg/700px-Wrigley_Field_is_ready_for_World_Series_Game_3._%2830525773952%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Wrigley Field (interior) \xe2\x80\x94 Game 3 of the 2016 World Series</div></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Rooftops" title="Wrigley Rooftops">Wrigley Rooftops</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field_renovations" title="Wrigley Field renovations">Wrigley Field renovations</a></div>\n<p>The Cubs have played their home games at <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a>, also known as <i>"The Friendly Confines"</i> since 1916. It was built in 1914 as <b>Weeghman Park</b> for the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Whales" title="Chicago Whales">Chicago Whales</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Federal_League" title="Federal League">Federal League</a> baseball team. The Cubs also shared the park with the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> of the NFL for 50 years. The ballpark includes a manual scoreboard, ivy-covered brick walls, and relatively small dimensions.\n</p><p>Located in Chicago\'s <a href="/wiki/Lake_View,_Chicago" title="Lake View, Chicago">Lake View</a> neighborhood, Wrigley Field sits on an irregular block bounded by Clark and Addison Streets and Waveland and Sheffield Avenues. The area surrounding the ballpark is typically referred to as Wrigleyville. There is a dense collection of sports bars and restaurants in the area, most with baseball inspired themes, including Sluggers, Murphy\'s Bleachers and <a href="/wiki/The_Cubby_Bear" title="The Cubby Bear">The Cubby Bear</a>. Many of the apartment buildings surrounding Wrigley Field on Waveland and Sheffield Avenues have built bleachers on their <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Rooftops" title="Wrigley Rooftops">rooftops</a> for fans to view games and other sell space for advertisement. One building on Sheffield Avenue has a sign atop its roof which says "Eamus Catuli!" which is <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for "Let\'s Go Cubs!" and another chronicles the time since the last Division title, pennant, and World Series championship. The 00 denotes the 2016 NL Central title, NL pennant, and the World Series championship. On game days, many residents rent out their yards and driveways to people looking for parking spots. The uniqueness of the neighborhood itself has ingrained itself into the culture of the Chicago Cubs as well as the Wrigleyville neighborhood, and has led to being used for concerts and other sporting events, such as the 2010 <a href="/wiki/NHL_Winter_Classic" title="NHL Winter Classic">NHL Winter Classic</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Blackhawks" title="Chicago Blackhawks">Chicago Blackhawks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Red_Wings" title="Detroit Red Wings">Detroit Red Wings</a>, as well as a 2010 <a href="/wiki/NCAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> men\'s football game between the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats" title="Northwestern Wildcats">Northwestern Wildcats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Fighting_Illini" title="Illinois Fighting Illini">Illinois Fighting Illini</a>.\n</p><p>In 2013, Tom Ricketts and team president Crane Kenney unveiled plans for a five-year, $575 million privately funded renovation of Wrigley Field.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Called the 1060 Project, the proposed plans included vast improvements to the stadium\'s facade, infrastructure, restrooms, concourses, suites, <a href="/wiki/Press_box" title="Press box">press box</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bullpen" title="Bullpen">bullpens</a>, and clubhouses, as well as a 6,000-square-foot (560&#160;m<sup>2</sup>)t <a href="/wiki/Jumbotron" title="Jumbotron">jumbotron</a> to be added in the left field bleachers, <a href="/wiki/Batting_cage" title="Batting cage">batting tunnels</a>, a 3,000-square-foot (280&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) video board in right field, and, eventually, an adjacent hotel, plaza, and office-retail complex.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> In previous years mostly all efforts to conduct any large-scale renovations to the field had been opposed by the city, former mayor <a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Daley" title="Richard M. Daley">Richard M. Daley</a> (a staunch White Sox fan), and especially the rooftop owners.\n</p><p>Months of negotiations between the team, a group of rooftop properties investors, local Alderman <a href="/wiki/Tom_Tunney" title="Tom Tunney">Tom Tunney</a>, and Chicago Mayor <a href="/wiki/Rahm_Emanuel" title="Rahm Emanuel">Rahm Emanuel</a> followed with the eventual endorsements of the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Chicago_Landmarks" title="Commission on Chicago Landmarks">Landmarks Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Plan_Commission" title="Chicago Plan Commission">Plan Commission</a> and final approval by the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_City_Council" title="Chicago City Council">Chicago City Council</a> in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The project began at the conclusion of the 2014 season.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bleacher_Bums">Bleacher Bums</span></h3>\n<p>The "<a href="/wiki/Bleacher_Bums" title="Bleacher Bums">Bleacher Bums</a>" is a name given to fans, many of whom spend much of the day heckling, who sit in the bleacher section at Wrigley Field. Initially, the group was called "bums" because it referred to a group of fans who were at most games, and since those games were all day game.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> A Broadway play,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> starring <a href="/wiki/Joe_Mantegna" title="Joe Mantegna">Joe Mantegna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Farina" title="Dennis Farina">Dennis Farina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Franz" title="Dennis Franz">Dennis Franz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/James_Belushi" class="mw-redirect" title="James Belushi">James Belushi</a> ran for years and was based on a group of Cub fans who frequented the club\'s games. The group was started in 1967 by dedicated fans Ron Grousl, Tom Nall and "mad bugler" <a href="/wiki/Mike_Murphy_(sports_radio_personality)" title="Mike Murphy (sports radio personality)">Mike Murphy</a>, who was a sports radio host during mid days on Chicago-based <a href="/wiki/WSCR" title="WSCR">WSCR</a> AM 670 "The Score". Murphy alleges that Grousl started the Wrigley tradition of throwing back opposing teams\' home run balls.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cubs_Win_Flag">Cubs Win Flag</span></h3>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Cubs_W_Flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Cubs_W_Flag.svg/220px-Cubs_W_Flag.svg.png" width="220" height="132" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Cubs_W_Flag.svg/330px-Cubs_W_Flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Cubs_W_Flag.svg/440px-Cubs_W_Flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="405" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Cubs Win Flag</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Cubs_L_Flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Cubs_L_Flag.svg/220px-Cubs_L_Flag.svg.png" width="220" height="132" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Cubs_L_Flag.svg/330px-Cubs_L_Flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Cubs_L_Flag.svg/440px-Cubs_L_Flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="405" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Cubs Lose Flag</div></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cubs_Win_Flag" title="Cubs Win Flag">Cubs Win Flag</a></div>\n<p>Beginning in the days of P.K. Wrigley and the 1937 bleacher/scoreboard reconstruction, and prior to modern media saturation, a flag with either a "W" or an "L" has flown from atop the scoreboard masthead, indicating the day\'s result(s) when baseball was played at Wrigley. In case of a split <a href="/wiki/Doubleheader_(baseball)" title="Doubleheader (baseball)">doubleheader</a>, both the "W" and "L" flags are flown.\n</p><p>Past Cubs media guides show that originally the flags were blue with a white "W" and white with a blue "L". In 1978, consistent with the dominant colors of the flags, blue and white lights were mounted atop the scoreboard, denoting "win" and "loss" respectively for the benefit of nighttime passers-by.\n</p><p>The flags were replaced by 1990, the first year in which the Cubs media guide reports the switch to the now familiar colors of the flags: White with blue "W" and blue with white "L". In addition to needing to replace the worn-out flags, by then the retired numbers of Banks and Williams were flying on the foul poles, as white with blue numbers; so the "good" flag was switched to match that scheme.\n</p><p>This long-established tradition has evolved to fans carrying the white-with-blue-W flags to both home and away games, and displaying them after a Cub win. The flags have become more and more popular each season since 1998, and are now even sold as T-shirts with the same layout. In 2009, the tradition spilled over to the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a> as <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Blackhawks" title="Chicago Blackhawks">Chicago Blackhawks</a> fans adopted a red and black "W" flag of their own.\n</p><p>During the early and mid-2000s, Chip Caray usually declared that a Cubs win at home meant it was <i>"White flag time at Wrigley!"</i>  More recently, the Cubs have promoted the phrase "Fly the W!" among fans and on social media.\n<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascots">Mascots</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clark-the-Cub-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Clark-the-Cub-01.jpg/220px-Clark-the-Cub-01.jpg" width="220" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Clark-the-Cub-01.jpg/330px-Clark-the-Cub-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Clark-the-Cub-01.jpg/440px-Clark-the-Cub-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2760" data-file-height="3452" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clark-the-Cub-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clark (left) with the Oriole Bird</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Clark_(mascot)" title="Clark (mascot)">Clark (mascot)</a></div>\n<p>The official Cubs team <a href="/wiki/Mascot" title="Mascot">mascot</a> is a young bear cub, named <a href="/wiki/Clark_(mascot)" title="Clark (mascot)">Clark</a>, described by the team\'s press release as a young and friendly Cub. Clark made his debut at Advocate Health Care on January 13, 2014, the same day as the press release announcing his installation as the club\'s first ever official physical mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The bear cub itself was used in the clubs since the early 1900s and was the inspiration of the Chicago Staleys changing their team\'s name to the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a>, because the Cubs allowed the football team to play at Wrigley Field in the 1930s.\n</p><p>The Cubs had no official physical mascot prior to Clark, though a man in a \'polar bear\' looking outfit, called "The Bear-man" (or Beeman), which was mildly popular with the fans, paraded the stands briefly in the early 1990s. There is no record of whether or not he was just a fan in a costume or employed by the club.  Through the 2013 season, there were "Cubbie-bear" mascots outside of Wrigley on game day, but none were employed by the team. They pose for pictures with fans for tips. The most notable of these was "Billy Cub" who worked outside of the stadium for over six years until July 2013, when the club asked him to stop. Billy Cub, who is played by fan John Paul Weier, had unsuccessfully petitioned the team to become the official mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another unofficial but much more well-known mascot is <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Woo_Woo" title="Ronnie Woo Woo">Ronnie "Woo Woo" Wickers</a><sup id="cite_ref-A_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> who is a longtime fan and local celebrity in the Chicago area. He is known to Wrigley Field visitors for his idiosyncratic cheers at baseball games, generally punctuated with an exclamatory "Woo!" (e.g., "Cubs, woo! Cubs, woo! Big-Z, woo! <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Zambrano_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos Zambrano (baseball)">Zambrano</a>, woo! Cubs, woo!") Longtime Cubs announcer <a href="/wiki/Harry_Caray" title="Harry Caray">Harry Caray</a> dubbed Wickers "Leather Lungs" for his ability to shout for hours at a time.<sup id="cite_ref-D_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> He is not employed by the team, although the club has on two separate occasions allowed him into the broadcast booth and allow him some degree of freedom once he purchases or is given a ticket by fans to get into the games. He is largely allowed to roam the park and interact with fans by Wrigley Field security.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>\n<p>During the summer of 1969, a Chicago studio group produced a single record called "Hey Hey! Holy Mackerel! (The Cubs Song)" whose title and lyrics incorporated the catch-phrases of the respective TV and radio announcers for the Cubs, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Brickhouse" title="Jack Brickhouse">Jack Brickhouse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vince_Lloyd" title="Vince Lloyd">Vince Lloyd</a>. Several members of the Cubs recorded an album called <i>Cub Power</i> which contained a cover of the song. The song received a good deal of local airplay that summer, associating it very strongly with that bittersweet season. It was played much less frequently thereafter, although it remained an unofficial Cubs theme song for some years after.\n</p><p>For many years, Cubs radio broadcasts started with "It\'s a Beautiful Day for a Ball Game" by the Harry Simeone Chorale. In 1979, Roger Bain released a 45 rpm record of his song "Thanks Mr. Banks", to honor "Mr. Cub" Ernie Banks.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The song "<a href="/wiki/Go,_Cubs,_Go" title="Go, Cubs, Go">Go, Cubs, Go!</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Goodman" title="Steve Goodman">Steve Goodman</a> was recorded early in the 1984 season, and was heard frequently during that season. Goodman died in September of that year, four days before the Cubs clinched the National League Eastern Division title, their first title in 39 years. Since 1984, the song started being played from time to time at <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a>; since 2007, the song has been played over the loudspeakers following each Cubs home victory.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/The_Mountain_Goats" title="The Mountain Goats">The Mountain Goats</a> recorded a song entitled "Cubs in Five" on its 1995 EP <a href="/wiki/Nine_Black_Poppies" title="Nine Black Poppies">Nine Black Poppies</a> which refers to the seeming impossibility of the Cubs winning a World Series in both its title and Chorus.\n</p><p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Jam" title="Pearl Jam">Pearl Jam</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Vedder" title="Eddie Vedder">Eddie Vedder</a> composed a song dedicated to the team called "<a href="/wiki/All_the_Way_(Eddie_Vedder_song)" title="All the Way (Eddie Vedder song)">All the Way</a>". Vedder, a Chicago native, and lifelong Cubs fan, composed the song at the request of Ernie Banks.\nPearl Jam has played this song live multiple times several of which occurring at Wrigley Field.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Eddie Vedder has played this song live twice, at his solo shows at the Chicago Auditorium on August 21 and 22, 2008.\n</p><p>An album entitled <i>Take Me Out to a Cubs Game</i> was released in 2008. It is a collection of 17 songs and other recordings related to the team,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Harry_Caray" title="Harry Caray">Harry Caray</a>\'s final performance of "<a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Out_to_the_Ball_Game" title="Take Me Out to the Ball Game">Take Me Out to the Ball Game</a>" on September 21, 1997, the Steve Goodman song mentioned above, and a newly recorded rendition of "<a href="/wiki/Talkin%27_Baseball" title="Talkin&#39; Baseball">Talkin\' Baseball</a>" (subtitled "Baseball and the Cubs") by <a href="/wiki/Terry_Cashman" title="Terry Cashman">Terry Cashman</a>. The album was produced in celebration of the 100th anniversary of the Cubs\' <a href="/wiki/1908_World_Series" title="1908 World Series">1908 World Series</a> victory and contains sounds and songs of the Cubs and Wrigley Field.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TMOTACGC_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMOTACGC-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span></h3>\n<p>The 1986 film <i><a href="/wiki/Ferris_Bueller%27s_Day_Off" title="Ferris Bueller&#39;s Day Off">Ferris Bueller\'s Day Off</a></i> showed a game played by the Cubs when Ferris\' principal goes to a bar looking for him.\n</p><p>The 1989 film <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_Part_II" title="Back to the Future Part II">Back to the Future Part II</a></i> depicts the Chicago Cubs defeating a baseball team from <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Series" title="2015 World Series">2015 World Series</a>, ending the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_franchise_postseason_droughts#Longest_current_World_Series_championship_drought" title="List of Major League Baseball franchise postseason droughts">longest championship drought</a> in all four of the major <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">North American professional sports leagues</a>. In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a> failed to make the playoffs but the Cubs were able to make it to the <a href="/wiki/2015_National_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2015 National League Wild Card Game">2015 National League Wild Card</a> round and move on to the <a href="/wiki/2015_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2015 National League Championship Series">2015 National League Championship Series</a> by October 21, 2015, the date where protagonist <a href="/wiki/Marty_McFly" title="Marty McFly">Marty McFly</a> traveled to the future in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> However, it was on October 21 that the Cubs were swept by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2015 National League Championship Series">NLCS</a>.\n</p><p>The 1993 film <i><a href="/wiki/Rookie_of_the_Year_(film)" title="Rookie of the Year (film)">Rookie of the Year</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Stern_(actor)" title="Daniel Stern (actor)">Daniel Stern</a>, centers on the Cubs as a team going nowhere into August when the team chances upon 12-year-old Cubs fan Henry Rowengartner (<a href="/wiki/Thomas_Ian_Nicholas" title="Thomas Ian Nicholas">Thomas Ian Nicholas</a>), whose right (throwing) arm tendons have healed tightly after a broken arm and granted him the ability to regularly pitch at speeds in excess of 100 miles per hour (160&#160;km/h). Following the Cubs\' win over the Cleveland Indians in Game 7 of the 2016 World Series, Nicholas, in celebration, tweeted the final shot from the movie: Henry holding his fist up to the camera to show a Cubs World Series ring.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tinker_to_Evers_to_Chance">Tinker to Evers to Chance</span></h3>\n<p><i>"<a href="/wiki/Baseball%27s_Sad_Lexicon" title="Baseball&#39;s Sad Lexicon">Baseball\'s Sad Lexicon</a>,"</i> also known as <i>"Tinker to Evers to Chance"</i> after its refrain, is a 1910 <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> <a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poem</a> by <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Pierce_Adams" class="mw-redirect" title="Franklin Pierce Adams">Franklin Pierce Adams</a>. The poem is presented as a single, rueful stanza from the point of view of a <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a> fan seeing the talented Chicago Cubs infield of <a href="/wiki/Shortstop" title="Shortstop">shortstop</a> <a href="/wiki/Joe_Tinker" title="Joe Tinker">Joe Tinker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_baseman" title="Second baseman">second baseman</a> <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Evers" title="Johnny Evers">Johnny Evers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/First_baseman" title="First baseman">first baseman</a> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Chance" title="Frank Chance">Frank Chance</a> complete a <a href="/wiki/Double_play" title="Double play">double play</a>. The trio began playing together with the Cubs in 1902, and formed a double play combination that lasted through April 1912. The Cubs won the pennant four times between 1906 and 1910, often defeating the Giants en route to the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>.</p><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;max-width:237px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:77px;max-width:77px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Tinker_baseball_card.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Tinker_baseball_card.jpg/75px-Tinker_baseball_card.jpg" width="75" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Tinker_baseball_card.jpg/113px-Tinker_baseball_card.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Tinker_baseball_card.jpg/150px-Tinker_baseball_card.jpg 2x" data-file-width="574" data-file-height="1024" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:77px;max-width:77px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Evers_baseball_card.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Evers_baseball_card.jpg/75px-Evers_baseball_card.jpg" width="75" height="132" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Evers_baseball_card.jpg/113px-Evers_baseball_card.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Evers_baseball_card.jpg/150px-Evers_baseball_card.jpg 2x" data-file-width="584" data-file-height="1024" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:77px;max-width:77px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Frank_Chance_Baseball_Card.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Frank_Chance_Baseball_Card.jpg/75px-Frank_Chance_Baseball_Card.jpg" width="75" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Frank_Chance_Baseball_Card.jpg/113px-Frank_Chance_Baseball_Card.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Frank_Chance_Baseball_Card.jpg/150px-Frank_Chance_Baseball_Card.jpg 2x" data-file-width="355" data-file-height="640" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Joe Tinker, Johnny Evers, and Frank Chance are the three Cubs described in the poem.</div></div></div>\n<blockquote>\n<dl><dd>These are the saddest of possible words:</dd>\n<dd>"Tinker to Evers to Chance."</dd>\n<dd>Trio of bear cubs, and fleeter than birds,</dd>\n<dd>Tinker and Evers and Chance.</dd>\n<dd>Ruthlessly pricking our gonfalon bubble,</dd>\n<dd>Making a Giant hit into a double \xe2\x80\x93</dd>\n<dd>Words that are heavy with nothing but trouble:</dd>\n<dd>"Tinker to Evers to Chance."</dd></dl>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The poem was first published in the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Evening_Mail" title="New York Evening Mail">New York Evening Mail</a></i> on July 12, 1912. Popular among <a href="/wiki/Sportswriter" class="mw-redirect" title="Sportswriter">sportswriters</a>, numerous additional verses were written. The poem gave Tinker, Evers, and Chance increased popularity and has been credited with their elections to the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">National Baseball Hall of Fame</a> in 1946.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Playoffs.2FChampionships"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Playoffs/Championships">Playoffs/Championships</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/National_League_Division_Series" title="National League Division Series">National League Division Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_division_winners" title="Major League Baseball division winners">Major League Baseball division winners</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_League_pennant_winners" title="List of National League pennant winners">List of National League pennant winners</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">List of World Series champions</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:95%; style="background-color:#CC3433;color:#FFFFFF;;">Total\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#CC3433;color:#FFFFFF;;">Wild Cards<br />Division titles\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#CC3433;color:#FFFFFF;;">2<br />7\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#CC3433;color:#FFFFFF;;">Division Series titles\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#CC3433;color:#FFFFFF;;">4\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#CC3433;color:#FFFFFF;;">NL pennants\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#CC3433;color:#FFFFFF;;">17\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#CC3433;color:#FFFFFF;;">World Series titles\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#CC3433;color:#FFFFFF;;">3\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<ul><li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><sup>a</sup></span>  Prior to 1969, divisions did not exist in MLB. The Chicago Cubs played in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a> between 1969\xe2\x80\x931993 before moving to the newly created <a href="/wiki/National_League_Central" title="National League Central">National League Central</a> in 1994.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_b"><sup>b</sup></span>  Prior to 1995, only two divisions existed in each league. With the realignment into three divisions and the institution of the wild card in 1995, the Division Series was added. <i><a href="/wiki/Division_Series" title="Division Series">Division Series</a></i>.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_c"><sup>c</sup></span>  Prior to 1969, the National League champion was determined by the best win\xe2\x80\x93loss record at the end of the regular season. <i>See <a href="/wiki/League_Championship_Series" title="League Championship Series">League Championship Series</a></i>.</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_d"><sup>d</sup></span>  None of the World Series contested before 1903 are recognized by MLB. <i>See <a href="/wiki/List_of_pre-World_Series_baseball_champions" title="List of pre-World Series baseball champions">List of pre-World Series baseball champions</a></i>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distinctions">Distinctions</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chicago_Cubs_seasons" title="List of Chicago Cubs seasons">List of Chicago Cubs seasons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs_award_winners_and_league_leaders" title="Chicago Cubs award winners and league leaders">Chicago Cubs award winners and league leaders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs_team_records" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago Cubs team records">Chicago Cubs team records</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chicago_Cubs_no-hitters" title="List of Chicago Cubs no-hitters">List of Chicago Cubs no-hitters</a></div>\n<p>Throughout the history of the Chicago Cubs\' franchise, fifteen different Cubs pitchers have pitched <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitters</a>; however, no Cubs pitcher has thrown a <a href="/wiki/Perfect_game" title="Perfect game">perfect game</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forbes_value_rankings"><i>Forbes</i> value rankings</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Forbes%27_list_of_the_most_valuable_sports_teams" title="Forbes&#39; list of the most valuable sports teams">Forbes\' list of the most valuable sports teams</a></div>\n<p>As of 2017, the Chicago Cubs are ranked as the 18th most valuable sports team in the world, 14th in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, fourth in MLB behind the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, and second in the city of <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> behind the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Bears</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_2017_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_2017-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:95%; text-align:center;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color:#273B81;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #CC3433, inset -2px -2px 0 #CC3433; -webkit-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #CC3433, inset -2px -2px 0 #CC3433; box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #CC3433, inset -2px -2px 0 #CC3433;;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#273B81;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #CC3433, inset -2px -2px 0 #CC3433; -webkit-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #CC3433, inset -2px -2px 0 #CC3433; box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #CC3433, inset -2px -2px 0 #CC3433;;">World\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#273B81;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #CC3433, inset -2px -2px 0 #CC3433; -webkit-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #CC3433, inset -2px -2px 0 #CC3433; box-shadow: Major League Baseball team rosters">All MLB rosters</a></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><br />\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_retired_numbers" title="List of Major League Baseball retired numbers">List of Major League Baseball retired numbers</a></div>\n<p>The Chicago Cubs retired numbers are commemorated on pinstriped flags flying from the foul poles at Wrigley Field, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a> player whose number 42 was <a href="/wiki/Retired" class="mw-redirect" title="Retired">retired</a> for all clubs. The first retired number flag, Ernie Banks\' number 14, was raised on the left field pole, and they have alternated since then. 14, 10 and 31 (Jenkins) fly on the left field pole; and 26, 23 and 31 (Maddux) fly on the right field pole.\n</p>\n<table style="white-space:nowrap"><tbody><tr><td>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cubs_10_Santo.svg" class="image"><img alt="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Cubs_10_Santo.svg/100px-Cubs_10_Santo.svg.png" width="100" height="57" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Cubs_10_Santo.svg/150px-Cubs_10_Santo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Cubs_10_Santo.svg/200px-Cubs_10_Santo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="402" data-file-height="229" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Ron_Santo" title="Ron Santo">Ron<br />Santo</a><br />3B<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Retired <span style="white-space:nowrap"><br />September 28, 2003</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cubs_14_Banks.svg" class="image"><img alt="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Cubs_14_Banks.svg/100px-Cubs_14_Banks.svg.png" width="100" height="57" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Cubs_14_Banks.svg/150px-Cubs_14_Banks.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Cubs_14_Banks.svg/200px-Cubs_14_Banks.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="402" data-file-height="229" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Ernie_Banks" title="Ernie Banks">Ernie<br />Banks</a><br />SS, 1B<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Retired <span style="white-space:nowrap"><br />May 3, 2009</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cubs_42_Robinson.svg" class="image"><img alt="42" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Cubs_42_Robinson.svg/100px-Cubs_42_Robinson.svg.png" width="100" height="57" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Cubs_42_Robinson.svg/150px-Cubs_42_Robinson.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Cubs_42_Robinson.svg/200px-Cubs_42_Robinson.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="402" data-file-height="229" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie<br />Robinson</a>*<br />2B<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Honored <span style="white-space:nowrap">April 15, 1997</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<ul><li>There is also a movement to retire numbers for other players, most notably the uniform shirt of <a href="/wiki/Gabby_Hartnett" title="Gabby Hartnett">Gabby Hartnett</a>. The Cubs first wore numbers on their shirts in 1932, and Hartnett wore #7 initially but switched to #9 for the next four seasons. From 1937 to 1940 he wore #2, which is the number considered for retirement. Petitions have been sent in to the team for <a href="/wiki/Cap_Anson" title="Cap Anson">Cap Anson</a> (shirt), <a href="/wiki/Hack_Wilson" title="Hack Wilson">Hack Wilson</a> (shirt), <a href="/wiki/Phil_Cavarretta" title="Phil Cavarretta">Phil Cavarretta</a> (3), <a href="/wiki/Andre_Dawson" title="Andre Dawson">Andre Dawson</a> (8) and, as well as more recent departures <a href="/wiki/Kerry_Wood" title="Kerry Wood">Kerry Wood</a> (34), <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Sosa" title="Sammy Sosa">Sammy Sosa</a> (21), and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Grace" title="Mark Grace">Mark Grace</a> (17).</li></ul>\n<p>* Robinson\'s number was retired by all MLB clubs.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hall_of_Famers">Hall of Famers</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote href="/wiki/Freddie_Lindstrom" title="Freddie Lindstrom">Freddie Lindstrom</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Rabbit_Maranville" title="Rabbit Maranville">Rabbit Maranville</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Greg_Maddux" title="Greg Maddux">Greg Maddux</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Joe_McCarthy_(manager)" title="Joe McCarthy (manager)">Joe McCarthy</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Hank_O%27Day" title="Hank O&#39;Day">Hank O\'Day</a><sup>3</sup><br /><a href="/wiki/Robin_Roberts_(baseball)" title="Robin Roberts (baseball)">Robin Roberts</a><br /><b><a href="/wiki/Ryne_Sandberg" title="Ryne Sandberg">Ryne Sandberg</a></b><br /><b><a href="/wiki/Ron_Santo" title="Ron Santo">Ron Santo</a></b>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Frank_Selee" title="Frank Selee">Frank Selee</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Albert_Spalding" title="Albert Spalding">Albert Spalding</a><sup>\xe2\x80\xa02</sup><br /><a href="/wiki/Bruce_Sutter" title="Bruce Sutter">Bruce Sutter</a>**<br /><b><a href="/wiki/Joe_Tinker" title="Joe Tinker">Joe Tinker</a></b>*<br /><a href="/wiki/Rube_Waddell" title="Rube Waddell">Rube Waddell</a><br /><a style="margin: 1em auto;display:none">\n<caption>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td>\n<td player-manager</li>\n<li><sup>3</sup> \xe2\x80\x93 inducted as umpire; played for Cubs or was player-manager</li></ul>\n</div>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:center; background-color:#273B81;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #CC3433, inset -2px -2px 0 #CC3433; -webkit-box-shadow: inset Iowa</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>AA</i>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Smokies" title="Tennessee Smokies">Tennessee Smokies</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Southern_League_(baseball)" title="Southern League (baseball)">Southern League</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Sevierville,_Tennessee" title="Sevierville, Tennessee">Sevierville, Tennessee</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Advanced A</i>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Myrtle_Beach_Pelicans" title="Myrtle Beach Pelicans">Myrtle Beach Pelicans</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Carolina_League" title="Carolina League">Carolina League</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina" title="Myrtle Beach, South Carolina">Myrtle Beach, South Carolina</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>A</i>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/South_Bend_Cubs" title="South Bend Cubs">South Bend Cubs</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Midwest_League" title="Midwest League">Midwest League</a>\n</td>\n<td><a
