Oregon</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="3"><i>Rookie</i>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Arizona_League_Cubs" title="Arizona League Cubs">AZL Cubs</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Arizona_League" title="Arizona League">Arizona League</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Mesa,_Arizona" title="Mesa, Arizona">Mesa, Arizona</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Dominican_Summer_League_Cubs" title="Dominican Summer League Cubs">DSL Cubs 1</a>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Dominican_Summer_League" title="Dominican Summer League">Dominican Summer League</a>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Boca_Chica" title="Boca Chica">Boca Chica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Dominican_Summer_League_Cubs" title="Dominican Summer League Cubs">DSL Cubs 2</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Before signing a developmental agreement with the Kane County Cougars in 2012, the Cubs had a Class A minor league affiliation on two occasions with the <a href="/wiki/Peoria_Chiefs" title="Peoria Chiefs">Peoria Chiefs</a> (1985\xe2\x80\x931995 and 2004\xe2\x80\x932012). <a href="/wiki/Ryne_Sandberg" title="Ryne Sandberg">Ryne Sandberg</a> managed the Chiefs from 2006 to 2010. In the period between those associations with the Chiefs the club had affiliations with the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Dragons" title="Dayton Dragons">Dayton Dragons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lansing_Lugnuts" title="Lansing Lugnuts">Lansing Lugnuts</a>. The Lugnuts were often affectionately referred to by <a href="/wiki/Chip_Caray" title="Chip Caray">Chip Caray</a> as "<a href="/wiki/Steve_Stone_(baseball)" title="Steve Stone (baseball)">Steve Stone</a>\'s favorite team." The 2007 developmental contract with the Tennessee Smokies was preceded by Double A affiliations with the <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Cubs" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando Cubs">Orlando Cubs</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Tenn_Diamond_Jaxx" class="mw-redirect" title="West Tenn Diamond Jaxx">West Tenn Diamond Jaxx</a>. On September 16, 2014 the Cubs announced a move of their top Class A affiliate from Daytona in the Florida State League to <a href="/wiki/Myrtle_Beach_Pelicans" title="Myrtle Beach Pelicans">Myrtle Beach</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_League" title="Carolina League">Carolina League</a> for the 2015 season.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Two days later, the Cubs signed a four-year player development contract with the <a href="/wiki/South_Bend_Silver_Hawks" class="mw-redirect" title="South Bend Silver Hawks">South Bend Silver Hawks</a> of the Midwest League, ending their brief relationship with the Kane County Cougars and shortly thereafter renaming the Silver Hawks the <a href="/wiki/South_Bend_Cubs" title="South Bend Cubs">South Bend Cubs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spring_training_history">Spring training history</span></h3>\n<p>The Chicago White Stockings, (today\'s Chicago Cubs), began spring training in <a href="/wiki/Hot_Springs,_Arkansas" title="Hot Springs, Arkansas">Hot Springs, Arkansas</a> in 1886. President <a href="/wiki/Albert_Spalding" title="Albert Spalding">Albert Spalding</a> (founder of Spalding Sporting Goods) and player/manager <a href="/wiki/Cap_Anson" title="Cap Anson">Cap Anson</a> brought their players to Hot Springs and played at the Hot Springs Baseball Grounds. The concept was for the players to have training and fitness before the start of the regular season, utilizing the bath houses of Hot Springs after practices.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-encyclopediaofarkansas.net_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopediaofarkansas.net-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> After the White Stockings had a successful season in 1886, winning the National League Pennant, other teams began bringing their players to Hot Springs for "spring training".<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopediaofarkansas.net_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopediaofarkansas.net-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The Chicago Cubs, <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Browns" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Browns">St. Louis Browns</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Spiders" title="Cleveland Spiders">Cleveland Spiders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Highlanders" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Highlanders">New York Highlanders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> were among the early squads to arrive. <a href="/wiki/Whittington_Park_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Whittington Park (baseball)">Whittington Park</a> (1894) and later <a href="/wiki/Majestic_Park_(baseball)" title="Majestic Park (baseball)">Majestic Park</a> (1909) and <a href="/wiki/Fogel_Field" title="Fogel Field">Fogel Field</a> (1912) were all built in Hot Springs specifically to host Major League teams.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Cubs\' current spring training facility is located in <a href="/wiki/Sloan_Park" title="Sloan Park">Sloan Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mesa,_Arizona" title="Mesa, Arizona">Mesa, Arizona</a>, where they play in the <a href="/wiki/Cactus_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Cactus League">Cactus League</a>. The park seats 15,000, making it Major League baseball\'s largest spring training facility by capacity. The Cubs annually sell out most of their games both at home and on the road. Before Sloan Park opened in 2014, the team played games at <a href="/wiki/HoHoKam_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="HoHoKam Park">HoHoKam Park</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Dwight Patterson Field from 1979. "HoHoKam" is literally translated from Native American as "those who vanished." The North Siders have called Mesa their spring home for most seasons since 1952.\n</p><p>In addition to Mesa, the club has held spring training in <a href="/wiki/Hot_Springs,_Arkansas" title="Hot Springs, Arkansas">Hot Springs, Arkansas</a> (1886, 1896\xe2\x80\x931900), (1909\xe2\x80\x931910) <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_New_Orleans#Baseball" title="Sports in New Orleans">New Orleans</a> (1870, 1907, 1911\xe2\x80\x931912); <a href="/wiki/Champaign,_Illinois" title="Champaign, Illinois">Champaign, Illinois</a> (1901\xe2\x80\x9302, 1906); Los Angeles (1903\xe2\x80\x9304, 1948\xe2\x80\x931949), <a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California" title="Santa Monica, California">Santa Monica, California</a> (1905); <a href="/wiki/French_Lick,_Indiana" title="French Lick, Indiana">French Lick, Indiana</a> (1908, 1943\xe2\x80\x931945); <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a> (1913\xe2\x80\x931916); <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a> (1917\xe2\x80\x931921); <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catalina_Island,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Catalina Island, California">Santa Catalina Island, California</a> (1922\xe2\x80\x931942, 1946\xe2\x80\x931947, 1950\xe2\x80\x931951); Rendezvous Park in <a href="/wiki/Mesa,_Arizona" title="Mesa, Arizona">Mesa</a> (1952\xe2\x80\x931965); <a href="/wiki/Blair_Field" title="Blair Field">Blair Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_California" title="Long Beach, California">Long Beach, California</a> (1966); and <a href="/wiki/Scottsdale,_Arizona" title="Scottsdale, Arizona">Scottsdale, Arizona</a> (1967\xe2\x80\x931978).\n</p><p>The curious location on Catalina Island stemmed from Cubs owner William Wrigley Jr.\'s then-majority interest in the island in 1919. Wrigley constructed a ballpark on the island to house the Cubs in spring training: it was built to the same dimensions as Wrigley Field. The ballpark was called Wrigley Field of Avalon.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> (The ballpark is long gone, but a clubhouse built by Wrigley to house the Cubs exists as the Catalina County Club.) However, by 1951 the team chose to leave Catalina Island and spring training was shifted to Mesa, Arizona.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The Cubs\' 30-year association with Catalina is chronicled in the book, <i>The Cubs on Catalina</i>, by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Vitti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jim Vitti (page does not exist)">Jim Vitti</a>, which was named International \'Book of the Year\' by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sporting_News" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sporting News">The Sporting News</a></i>. The Cubs left Catalina after some bad weather in 1951, choosing to move to Mesa, a city where the Wrigleys also had interests.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Today, there is an exhibit at the Catalina Museum dedicated to the Cubs\' spring training on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The former location in Mesa is actually the second HoHoKam Park; the first was built in 1976 as the spring-training home of the Oakland Athletics who left the park in 1979. Apart from HoHoKam Park and Sloan Park the Cubs also have another Mesa training facility called Fitch Park, this complex provides 25,000 square feet (2,300&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of team facilities, including major league clubhouse, four practice fields, one practice infield, enclosed batting tunnels, batting cages, a maintenance facility, and administrative offices for the Cubs.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span></h3>\n<p>Cubs radio rights are held by <a href="/wiki/CBS_Radio" title="CBS Radio">CBS Radio</a>; its acquisition of the radio rights effective 2015 ended the team\'s 90-year association with <a href="/wiki/WGN_(AM)" title="WGN (AM)">720 WGN</a>. During the first season of the contract, Cubs games aired on <a href="/wiki/WBBM_(AM)" title="WBBM (AM)">WBBM</a>, taking over as flagship of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs_Radio_Network" title="Chicago Cubs Radio Network">Chicago Cubs Radio Network</a>. On November 11, 2015, CBS announced that the Cubs would move to WBBM\'s all-sports sister station, <a href="/wiki/WSCR_(AM)" class="mw-redirect" title="WSCR (AM)">WSCR</a>, beginning in the 2016 season. The move was enabled by WSCR\'s end of their rights agreement for the White Sox, who moved to <a href="/wiki/WLS_(AM)" title="WLS (AM)">WLS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-suntimes-cubswscr_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suntimes-cubswscr-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The play-by-play voice of the Cubs is <a href="/wiki/Pat_Hughes_(sportscaster)" title="Pat Hughes (sportscaster)">Pat Hughes</a>, who has held the position since 1996, joined by <a href="/wiki/Ron_Coomer" title="Ron Coomer">Ron Coomer</a>. Former Cubs third baseman and fan favorite <a href="/wiki/Ron_Santo" title="Ron Santo">Ron Santo</a> had been Hughes\' long-time partner until his death in 2010. <a href="/wiki/Keith_Moreland" title="Keith Moreland">Keith Moreland</a> replaced Hall of Fame inductee Santo for three seasons, followed by Coomer for the 2014 season.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Print">Print</span></h3>\n<p>The club also produces its own print media; the Cubs\' official magazine <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://chicago.cubs.mlb.com/chc/fan_forum/vineline.jsp"><i>Vineline</i></a>, which has 12 annual issues, is in its third decade, and spotlights players and events involving the club. The club also publishes a traditional <a href="/wiki/Media_guide" title="Media guide">media guide</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chicago_Cubs_broadcasters" title="List of Chicago Cubs broadcasters">List of Chicago Cubs broadcasters</a></div>\n<p>As of September 1, 2016, Cubs games air locally on the following outlets:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports_Chicago" title="NBC Sports Chicago">NBC Sports Chicago</a>, a cable network owned in part by <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal" title="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</a> and the Ricketts family. It broadcasts all Cubs games not broadcast over-the-air, or nationally by Major League Baseball\'s television partners.<sup id="cite_ref-cbj-cubs2015wgn_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbj-cubs2015wgn-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WGN-TV" title="WGN-TV">WGN-TV</a> (channel 9.1), a <a href="/wiki/Tribune_Media" title="Tribune Media">Tribune Media</a>-owned over-the-air station that has aired Cubs telecasts since its inception in 1948; WGN-TV\'s Cubs telecasts are produced by the station\'s sports department, <a href="/wiki/WGN_Sports" title="WGN Sports">WGN Sports</a>. In November 2013, the team exercised an option to terminate its existing deal with WGN-TV after the 2014 season, requesting a higher-valued contract lasting through the 2019 season (which would be aligned with the end of its contract with CSN Chicago). WGN-TV announced on January 7, 2015 that it would maintain broadcast rights to 45 Cubs games through the 2019 season within the Chicago market only.<sup id="cite_ref-cbj-cubs2015wgn_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbj-cubs2015wgn-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tribune-contractend_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tribune-contractend-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WLS-TV" title="WLS-TV">WLS-TV</a> (channel 7.1), an <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> owned-and-operated station. It was announced on December 12, 2014 that the station would acquire rights to 25 games per season through 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-tribune-closingin_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tribune-closingin-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wls-cubsaffiliates_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wls-cubsaffiliates-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Prior to September 1, 2016, when WGN-TV ended their CW affiliation to return to being an <a href="/wiki/Independent_station_(North_America)" title="Independent station (North America)">independent station</a>, several games in the WGN package since 2015 were sub-licensed to <a href="/wiki/Fox_Television_Stations" title="Fox Television Stations">Fox Television Stations</a>-owned <a href="/wiki/MyNetworkTV" title="MyNetworkTV">MyNetworkTV</a> station <a href="/wiki/WPWR-TV" title="WPWR-TV">WPWR-TV</a> (channel 50.1), due to CW pre-emption limits which precluded airing on WGN-TV. These games returned full-time to WGN-TV upon that date, when WPWR assumed the market\'s CW affiliation and WGN was no longer limited by a network. In previous years, the sublicensed games were carried by <a href="/wiki/WCIU-TV" title="WCIU-TV">WCIU-TV</a> (channel 26.1) under the branding of "CubsNet" and "WGN Sports on The U".<sup id="cite_ref-trib-whitesoxwpwr_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trib-whitesoxwpwr-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>WGN\'s Cubs games formerly aired nationally on <a href="/wiki/WGN_America" title="WGN America">WGN America</a>; however, prior to the 2015 season, the Cubs, as well as all other Chicago sports programming, was dropped from the channel as part of its re-positioning as a general entertainment cable channel.<sup id="cite_ref-ccb-wgnanosports_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccb-wgnanosports-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> To compensate, all games carried by over-the-air channels are syndicated to a network of other television stations within the Cubs\' region, which includes Illinois and parts of Indiana and Iowa.<sup id="cite_ref-wls-cubsaffiliates_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wls-cubsaffiliates-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>All of the team\'s current television contracts end after the 2019 season.  On November 16, 2015 in an interview with <a href="/wiki/WSCR" title="WSCR">WSCR</a> radio, the Cubs\' president of business operations Crane Kenney stated that the team was seeking to launch its own in-house regional sports network.<sup id="cite_ref-cbj-cubs2015wgn_110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbj-cubs2015wgn-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usatoday-cubsrsn_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-cubsrsn-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Len_Kasper" title="Len Kasper">Len Kasper</a> has been the Cubs\' television <a href="/wiki/Play-by-play" class="mw-redirect" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a> announcer since 2005 and was joined by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Deshaies" title="Jim Deshaies">Jim Deshaies</a> in 2013. <a href="/wiki/Bob_Brenly" title="Bob Brenly">Bob Brenly</a> (analyst, 2005\xe2\x80\x9312), <a href="/wiki/Chip_Caray" title="Chip Caray">Chip Caray</a> (play-by-play, 1998\xe2\x80\x932004), <a href="/wiki/Steve_Stone_(baseball)" title="Steve Stone (baseball)">Steve Stone</a> (analyst, 1983\xe2\x80\x932000, 2003\xe2\x80\x9304), <a href="/wiki/Joe_Carter" title="Joe Carter">Joe Carter</a> (analyst for WGN-TV games, 2001\xe2\x80\x9302) and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Otto" title="Dave Otto">Dave Otto</a> (analyst for <a href="/wiki/FSN_Chicago" title="FSN Chicago">FSN Chicago</a> games, 2001\xe2\x80\x9302) also have spent time broadcasting from the Cubs booth since the death of Harry Caray in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ford_C._Frick_Award_recipients">Ford C. Frick Award recipients</span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours" style="font-size: 95%; margin: 1em auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color: #273B81; color: #FFFFFF; text-align: center;">Chicago Cubs <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Frick Award"><span style="color: #FFFFFF;">Ford C. Frick Award</span></a> recipients\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background-color: #CC3433; color: #FFFFFF; text-align: center;">Affiliation according to the National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<table style="margin: 1em auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Bob_Elson" title="Bob Elson">Bob Elson</a>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Jack_Brickhouse" title="Jack Brickhouse">Jack Brickhouse</a>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Harry_Caray" title="Harry Caray">Harry Caray</a>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Milo_Hamilton" title="Milo Hamilton">Milo Hamilton</a>\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li><b>Names in bold</b> received the award based primarily on their work as broadcasters for the Cubs.</li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li></ul>\n</div>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
